  <span id="freeText5407996463650191090" style="display:none">Holy mother of cliffhangers, I hate it when they do that!!<br /><br />Okay, you got me. I totally adore Ilona Andrews and wouldn’t fault them for a thing. <br /><br />Part of a Kate Daniels full BR with the <a href="””" rel="nofollow noopener">IAA</a>, Magic Strikes is the best KD novel yet. Seriously, better than book 2 and WAY better than book 1. There is <i>so much Curran</i> in this book and it is a feast for the mind and soul. There’s enough humor to fill the pages just based on Kate’s reaction to his name. <blockquote>
  <i>”So, how are things with you and Curran?”<br /><br />There were times in life when I wished for supreme mental powers. Like telekinesis. Mostly, I wanted them to crush my opponents. But right now I wanted them so I could pull the chair out from under Andrea and maker her fall on her butt.<br /><br />I settled for spitting three times over my left shoulder. </i>
</blockquote><br />There is also plenty of focus on Julie, Derek, Jim, and the ever-mysterious Roland, but those pale in comparison to the developing shitshow between Kate and Curran. She inadvertently let Curran wedge his foot in the door in Magic Burns when she ate food Curran offered her, which apparently is code for <b>“You’re the big strong lion-man I’ve chosen to protect me and rock my world”</b> in Curran-speak. Hilarity ensues as Kate continues to fend off his advances and fails spectacularly. I cannot wait to see where this goes. <br /><br />Magic Mourns is next on my tbr, hope it measures up.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1785656259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=my-library-catalogue">my-library-catalogue</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785656259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4136827574508977154">Kate Daniels is making a strong case to claim the spot as my favorite urban fantasy (to even be in contention is saying something – this genre is filled with authors that I absolutely love). I can’t believe how much better the second and third books have been. If it hadn’t been for my amazing Goodreads friends urging me to continue, it might have been years before I picked them up again.<br/><br/>Why do I now love it so much, you ask? Well, for one thing, the love story turned into a slowly developing seg</span>
  <span id="freeText4136827574508977154" style="display:none">Kate Daniels is making a strong case to claim the spot as my favorite urban fantasy (to even be in contention is saying something – this genre is filled with authors that I absolutely love). I can’t believe how much better the second and third books have been. If it hadn’t been for my amazing Goodreads friends urging me to continue, it might have been years before I picked them up again.<br /><br />Why do I now love it so much, you ask? Well, for one thing, the love story turned into a slowly developing segment that practically sizzles with romantic tension. It’s showcasing a fun dynamic between the characters that has me laughing out loud at every turn. I found this book in particular downright hysterical. Kate might be even funnier than Harry Dresden, if you can imagine. But the story also had a compelling mystery, which gave it the perfect balance of light and dark.<br /><br />Magic Strikes contained an arena-style competition (and if you’ve been following my blog for any length of time you probably know how much I LOVE books with featured competitions) which sent the book from great all the way to the stratosphere as far as I’m concerned. I’ve been really stingy with solid 5-star ratings lately, even going so far as to re-rate a bunch of 5-star titles down to a 4 or 4.5. I decided it has more of an impact to only give 5 stars to books that make my all-time favorites list. And you know what? Magic Strikes made the cut – I am already itching to go back and reread it!<br /><br />Other books you might like:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5585788.Skinwalker__Jane_Yellowrock___1_" title="Skinwalker (Jane Yellowrock, #1) by Faith Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Skinwalker</a> – Faith Hunter<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47212.Storm_Front__The_Dresden_Files___1_" title="Storm Front (The Dresden Files, #1) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Storm Front</a> – Jim Butcher<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71811.Moon_Called__Mercy_Thompson___1_" title="Moon Called (Mercy Thompson, #1) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Moon Called</a> – Patricia Briggs<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13507967.Dark_Currents__Agent_of_Hel___1_" title="Dark Currents (Agent of Hel, #1) by Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Currents</a> – Jacqueline Carey<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/793399.Stray__Shifters___1_" title="Stray (Shifters, #1) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">Stray</a> – Rachel Vincent<br /><br />Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nikiahawkes.com">www.nikiahawkes.com</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3487087265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10771720172453838393"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>Urban fantasy was my method of escape in college when I was frequently mentally exhausted from writing ten-page research papers and fatigued from pulling all-nighters. After reading endless books about psychiatric disorders, behaviorism, and the physical structures of the eye, sometimes it's nice to kick it with something that's just pure fun-- and for me, PNRs were always that. I will forever have a soft spot for vampires, shape-shifter</span>
  <span id="freeText10771720172453838393" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>Urban fantasy was my method of escape in college when I was frequently mentally exhausted from writing ten-page research papers and fatigued from pulling all-nighters. After reading endless books about psychiatric disorders, behaviorism, and the physical structures of the eye, sometimes it's nice to kick it with something that's just pure fun-- and for me, PNRs were always that. I will forever have a soft spot for vampires, shape-shifters, and witches.<br><br><br><br>The Kate Daniels series is basically the epitome of every book I loved as a woman in my only twenties, only upgraded, and equipped with a fancy sword. It borrows heavily from the folklore and mythology of <i>all </i>cultures (not just Western ones) and features a jaded, quippy heroine who the authors also aren't afraid to portray as emotionally vulnerable. MAGIC STRIKES, in particular, really delves deep into Kate's personal history and what makes her tick.<br><br><br><br>This book takes on a <i>Hunger Games</i>-like flavor when we learn about an underground fighting league that pits magical creature against magical creature in a high-stakes stadium tournament that frequently results in fights to the death-- only the price of defeat may be higher than anyone thought. Creatures are turning up dead and there's some sinister challengers who read as human but have abilities that no human would have, and things are bad enough that even Curran's Pack members are trying to undermine his authority, out of fear of starting an out-and-out territory war.<br><br><br><br>So you know, just another day in the world of Kate Daniels.<br><br><br><br>I didn't like this book <i>quite </i>as much as the previous book because this one was so brutal and violent and cutthroat. The other books in the series aren't exactly free from violence, but I must admit, I'm squeamish and I tend to balk at the presence of too much graphic physical violence. The gladiatorial elements were compelling though, and everything that happened in this book was relevant to the plot, but I was surprised at how much more violent it was than the previous too books. Poor Derek.<br><br><br><br>That said, I really appreciated how diverse this series was/is. Especially considering that it was published 10 years ago, before that was really the status quo and everything was overwhelmingly <i>white</i>. Andrews really makes an effort to be inclusive and while there are some stereotypes that have since become outmoded, it really stands out from its contemporaries, which tended to be way less diverse and feminist in tone. I love that Kate Daniels doesn't just fall over for a man, and she doesn't eschew femininity like Anita Blake did. I mean, she wears underwear with bows on! Love. Being a strong woman doesn't mean hating on feminine things. I'm glad to see Team Andrews gets that.<br><br><br><br>Also, Curran! I'm still Team Rogan for life, but this book made me realize why everyone loves him. That cliffhanger ending! I am DECEASED. Thank goodness I have books four and five on standby.<br><br><br><br>Definitely recommend this book to anyone who loves UF/PNRs but is tired of the same ol' same ol'.<br><br><br><br>3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10771720172453838393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1762101524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1762101524" />
    <a title="Haïfa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54721988-ha-fa"><img alt="Haïfa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592921740p2/54721988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1762101524?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haïfa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haïfa" href="/user/show/54721988-ha-fa">Haïfa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54721988-ha-fa?shelf=uf">uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54721988-ha-fa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54721988-ha-fa?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1762101524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer925173118434464520">I'm flying through this 3rd read! :D Favorite installment of the series.<br/>Full audiobook experience this time around. <br/><br/>Original, a bit rearranged, <b>spoiler-free</b> review below.<br/>___________________________________<br/><br/><b>I loved this book so much. It was near perfection!</b><br/><br/>And it took me 2 months to review... I don't even know where to start. I had a lot of <s>fangirling</s> thoughts and things to say about this one when I turned the last page. But I forgot it all. <br/><br/>What I know for sure is that it made me embark in an emo</span>
  <span id="freeText925173118434464520" style="display:none">I'm flying through this 3rd read! :D Favorite installment of the series.<br>Full audiobook experience this time around. <br><br>Original, a bit rearranged, <b>spoiler-free</b> review below.<br>___________________________________<br><br><b>I loved this book so much. It was near perfection!</b><br><br>And it took me 2 months to review... I don't even know where to start. I had a lot of <s>fangirling</s> thoughts and things to say about this one when I turned the last page. But I forgot it all. <br><br>What I know for sure is that it made me embark in an emotional roller-coaster ride and I don't remember the last time I cared this much about fictional characters. <b>It made me want to huddle under my blankets, drink hot chocolate and spend all day reading and re-reading it. And it made me laugh so hard.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"His Majesty needs a can-I girl anyway and I'm not it."<br>"A can-I girl?" Andrea frowned.<br>"Can I fetch you your food, Your Majesty? Can I tell you how strong and mighty you are, Your Majesty? Can I pick out your fleas, Your Majesty? Can I kiss your ass, Your Majesty? Can I ..." <br>It dawned on me that Raphael was sitting very still. Frozen, like a statue, his gaze fixed on the point above my head. <br>"He’s standing behind me, isn’t he?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The story was exciting and the plot fast-paced. New enemies threaten the Pack's (the Atlanta shapeshifters' pack) safety and once more, Kate gets entangled in the mess when Derek, her teenage shapeshifter sidekick, is badly injured. In order to save his life, she will have to juggle her position as the Order's representative, Curran (Beast lord, aka head of the Pack), the Midnight Games (an underground fighting tournament) and the mysterious forces that threaten the shapeshifters of Atlanta.<br><br>The Andrews have created such <b>an amazing panoply of great characters</b> in the last 2 books. And what I absolutely love about <i>Magic Strikes</i> is that these characters are all but frozen. We see them evolve, we see them learn, suffer, show a lot of potential and open up about their histories and luggage. In each book, we discover new facets of Kate, Curran, Derek, Jim, Andrea, Doolitle... while new characters appear and seamlessly find their spot in the big picture... and the result is so coherent it makes them look larger than life. It's just so freaking amazing. <br><br><b>Kate is a fantastic character</b>. When I started this series, I was afraid she would turn out to be a stereotype of the genre: badass, big-mouthed and acting all tough and scary and pushing people away. And in a way, she was all that at the beginning. <b>But not only!</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It was a matter of principle. If somebody sniped Saiman while I sat two feet away, I would have to pack up my knives and take up farming instead.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I love the fact that she is scarred, that she drags a difficult and heavy background. I love the fact that she's always questioning things, that she feels guilt, doubts, fear. I love the fact that she is cynical, self-mocking and so damn funny! I also love the fact that she is a bit insane and scary.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"And did you have to hack his arms off?"<br>"Yes, I did. He wouldn't go through the door."<br>"You say it like you're proud of it."<br>I was proud of it. It was an example of quick thinking in a difficult situation. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Again, the Andrews did their homework and again we have a new mythology inspired by the Indian folklore this time. This is very refreshing because as much as I'm familiar with, and love the Greek/Roman and Egyptian mythologies, most fictional works in the genre usually focus on them and it is always interesting to explore new cultures. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1574953440i/28524349._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Gorgeous new french cover</i><br><br>But my true weak spot for these books (and this one in particular) is the romance in it. To be honest, I don't read romance. It's a genre that never appealed to me... And yet, I find myself thrilled and dreamy and moved by the romance in this series. The building tension made me turn the pages at an alarmingly fast rate and feel like a teenager who had been asked for her first date. The dialogues are hilarious and we get to discover a funny, even childish at times, Beast Lord in this book. Kate's reaction to the weird shapeshifters' romantic standards, especially the breaking and entering, was priceless and, let's be honest, <b>healthy</b>. Yes, I'm looking at you, Bella Swan!<br><br>The only stain on this almost perfect book is the recurrent reminders and "re-explanations". I guess they're supposed to help a new reader, who starts in the middle of the series, understand the context and the background (how the magic works, the different factions of Atlanta, the functioning of the Pack, the shapeshifters' characteristics...). But for someone who devours the books in order, it gets tedious, slows the pace and makes me wanna turn the pages faster, but not for the good reasons... But it's a minor con for me to be honest. I just feel it's important to mention for future readers' sake. <br><br><b>Conclusion </b><br>This book was so freaking good I already re-read my favorite parts 5 times (it's been only 2 months since I first read it...). Fast-paced, thrilling, funny, intense and very gory in places as well. No wonder this installment seems to be, by consensus, the best book of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="925173118434464520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1015862448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015862448" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1015862448?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9740699-magic-strikes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015862448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14812001953314984948">13 April 2020: <a href='https://amzn.to/2V4FNN8' rel='nofollow noopener'>$1.99 on Kindle</a> - I don't recommend reading this series out of order, but this book is my FAVORITE in the series (though honestly, it is hard to rank them because the entire series is amazing and awesome).<br/><br/>June 2016 Re-read.<br/>July 2015 re-read: I love this book so much. <br/>August 2014 Re-read:<br/><br/>Apparently, I've never written a review of this book - though I've read it at least a couple dozen times. In fact, I distinctly remember the last re-read I did I had plans to review ALL the books i</span>
  <span id="freeText14812001953314984948" style="display:none">13 April 2020: <a href="https://amzn.to/2V4FNN8" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99 on Kindle</a> - I don't recommend reading this series out of order, but this book is my FAVORITE in the series (though honestly, it is hard to rank them because the entire series is amazing and awesome).<br /><br />June 2016 Re-read.<br />July 2015 re-read: I love this book so much. <br />August 2014 Re-read:<br /><br />Apparently, I've never written a review of this book - though I've read it at least a couple dozen times. In fact, I distinctly remember the last re-read I did I had plans to review ALL the books in the series. <br /><br />Then I hit this book, with its humor that keeps me laughing all the damn time, and the suspense that keeps me on the edge of my seat, biting my nails. And that ending! Good lord. *fans self* How could I be expected to write a review??<br /><br />But I'm going to try. I don't want to spoil anything so I'm pretty much going to devolve into fangirl squealing from here on out. Fair warning.<br /><br />I've said it before, and I'll say it again, this book is absolutely, mind-blowingly ... PERFECT. Every time I read it I can't stop. The humor that's on nearly every page makes me struggle against updating all the time, quoting it all. I laugh and grin like an idiot throughout damn near this entire book. You should see the looks I've gotten from perfect strangers. There are the moments when I'm ready to break into tears though. The struggle and dangers are very real in this world, and sometimes not everyone makes it.<br /><br />By now, I've come to love not only Kate and Curran, but everyone else in this messed up Post-Shift Atlanta. Derek, Julie, Jim, Raphael, Andrea and even Saiman. Then there's the new characters we meet, some that made me laugh, and one that made me freeze up in fear. I still get shivers when I read his entrance and introduction to Kate. The point is that I'm totally invested in these people, I feel like I'm fighting right there alongside them, struggling to survive - and more, fighting to <i>live</i>.<br /><br />The plot in <i>Magic Strikes</i> is one of the most interesting, tightly written, and beautifully executed I've seen. Every single thing has significance - you may not realize it at the time, but it's there. Each moment leading to a shattering conclusion where my heart's in my throat and I cheer when it's all over. <br /><br />I've thought about including some of my favorite quotes, but we'd be here all day. <br /><br />You know those things where people want you to name five desert-island-keepers? You know, the five books that you'd take with you to read and re-read with no other books available? I can never pick. Asking me to pick favorite books - narrowing them down - is so hard it's painful to me. But I can easily say that <i>Magic Strikes</i> would be one of them.<br /><br />20 July 2014: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B003QP4DVS/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=B003QP4DVS&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=touthenig-20&amp;linkId=EZHU44KXUOQ56C4Z" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99 on Kindle</a><br /><br />This is my favorite series ever!!! The entire series is on sale!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14812001953314984948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1544432951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544432951" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544432951?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544432951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5893218961070450"><b>"I gave him a smile. I was aiming for sweet, but he turned a shade paler and scooted a bit farther from me. Note to self: work more on sweet and less on psycho-killer."</b><br/><br/>This is the first book in this series that actually, truly, really struck me. The previus two were undeniably, deliciously funny, enjoyable, quick (I read each of them in one sitting) and <b>frustratingly cute </b>when it came to Kate and Curran, because, let's face it, this couple here is the ultimate level of everyhing definable as fru</span>
  <span id="freeText5893218961070450" style="display:none"><b>"I gave him a smile. I was aiming for sweet, but he turned a shade paler and scooted a bit farther from me. Note to self: work more on sweet and less on psycho-killer."</b><br /><br />This is the first book in this series that actually, truly, really struck me. The previus two were undeniably, deliciously funny, enjoyable, quick (I read each of them in one sitting) and <b>frustratingly cute </b>when it came to Kate and Curran, because, let's face it, this couple here is the ultimate level of everyhing definable as frustratingly cute.<br /><br />But, trying to keep my hormones in check, what is it that made <i>Magic Strikes</i> superior to its two predecessors?<br /><br />•First of all, finally, <i>finally</i> I'm beginning to perceive these <b>characters</b> as real people instead of just lifeless fictional doodles. In the previous book I had been able to grow attached only to Kate and Curran, whose personalities are so resolute and fierce as to leave you no choice but to side with and care for them. But the rest of the cast- that was kind of a problem for me. I wasn't invested of them, whether because I didn't know enough about them or because the way they were introduced and acted seemed unremarkable to me, I can't tell.<br />With this book, instead, things changed. I <b>cared</b> for everyone. Derek, Julie, Jim, Andrea, Raphael, Dali. It didn't matter if they appeared just in a few scenes, or if they said just a couple of lines, this time I was <b>feeling</b> them. I could <b>connect</b> with them. And, for me, how much I enjoy the characters almost always and almost perfectly reflects how much I enjoy the book as a whole.<br /><br />•Almost as if as a result of the characters not being particularly engaging, the element that in books one and two used to come more into focus was the <b>plot</b>. But I wasn't a great fan of that either: maybe influenced by a not exactly perfect world-building, the events of the story were a bit confused, many passages not completely clear, and thus my attention was a bit fluctuating. But the plot of <i>Magic Strikes</i> is not only more interesting, but more <b>fluid</b>, <b>enthralling</b>, and it <b>won't let you pause for breath</b>.<br /><br />•Last but not least, <b>Kate and Curran</b> (did you really think I would let it go without at least a few words about them?). I adored their interactions in this book. I adore their relationship. I adored that we actually get to see, step by step, how it develops, why it develops, what makes it develop. It's slow, so slow that you want to scream and destroy thing randomly, but we wouldn't love it if it wasn't like it, and we wouldn't love them were they not as stubborn as they happen to be. <br />My hope lies in you, guys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5893218961070450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer968591888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2354991820509636139"><b>First reread January 2015 - See review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156910548?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a></b>.<br/><br/>*********<br/><b>Original review (June 2014):</b><br/><br/><b>How much better can this series get!?</b> I’m seriously being blown away by every new instalment here. KD = pure awesomeness. Fabulous, exciting, memorable, astounding, staggering, wonderful, impressive, breathtaking, and nothing short of downright amazing. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418726472ra/12883198.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Ever went on a roller coaster ride?</b> Take that feeling, multiply it by 10 and you might get an idea of what this book is like. There is so much to take here that my h</span>
  <span id="freeText2354991820509636139" style="display:none"><b>First reread January 2015 - See review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156910548?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></b>.<br><br>*********<br><b>Original review (June 2014):</b><br><br><b>How much better can this series get!?</b> I’m seriously being blown away by every new instalment here. KD = pure awesomeness. Fabulous, exciting, memorable, astounding, staggering, wonderful, impressive, breathtaking, and nothing short of downright amazing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418726472ra/12883198.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ever went on a roller coaster ride?</b> Take that feeling, multiply it by 10 and you might get an idea of what this book is like. There is so much to take here that my heart must have stopped beating quite a few times as I was <s>reading</s> devouring Magic Strikes. The world building blew me away (again). It's even richer and more complex than in previous instalments. I didn’t think it was possible but yes, the Andrews got even better at it! This series is probably the better-crafted I have ever read. We had to wait for the third book in the series to find out about Kate’s blood and why she is so special but it was handled very well by the authors. Situations and characters take time to evolve and develop within the series but it doesn’t feel forced as all things are revealed in due time. There is still a lot to figure out about Kate though which leaves room for much more development in instalments to come.<br><br>I think what I like most about this series is that it is so well-balanced. <b>The action and battle scenes are mind-blowing</b> (and that’s saying a lot since I usually hate battle scenes), there is emotion, lots of humour, mystery, mythology… Everything really! <br><br><b>Oh and the characters!</b> Kate &amp; Curran are just great (I love that the romance part of the book is only a subplot so far and not taking over the whole series), the Derek situation is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[heartbreaking <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Saiman is a total creep but I love him, Julie &amp; Dali are both welcome additions to the cast of characters, I love Andrea, I love Raphael… As I said in a previous review I think I just love everything single character in this series, even the evil ones!<br><br><b>What else? The quotes! The quotes!</b> Sorry, I can't resist it.<blockquote>Seven pairs of glowing eyes stared at me: four green, three yellow. Judging by the glow, the shapeshifter crew hovered on the verge of going furry. One of their own was dead and they were out for blood. I kept my tone light. “You fellows ever thought of hiring out as a Christmas lights crew? You’d make a fortune.”</blockquote><blockquote>A shadow crossed Andrea’s face. “I don’t want to be his TWT-IHFB” “What does that mean?” “That Weird Thing I Haven’t Fucked Before.” I choked on a bite of gyro.</blockquote><blockquote>“His Majesty needs a can-I girl anyway. And I’m not it.” “A can-I girl?” Andrea frowned. I leaned back. “Can I fetch you your food, Your Majesty? Can I tell you how strong and mighty you are, Your Majesty? Can I pick out your fleas, Your Majesty? Can I kiss your ass, Your Majesty? Can I…” It dawned on me that Raphael was sitting very still. Frozen, like a statue, his gaze fixed on the point above my head. “He’s standing behind me, isn’t he?” Andrea nodded slowly. “Technically it should be “may I,” Curran said, his voice deeper than I remembered. “Since you’re asking permission.” Why me? “To answer your question, yes, you may kiss my ass. Normally I prefer to maintain my personal space, but you’re a Friend of the Pack and your services have proven useful once or twice. I strive to accommodate the wishes of persons friendly to my people. My only question is, would your kissing my ass be obeisance, grooming, or foreplay?”</blockquote><blockquote>Saiman sighed. “At the risk of sounding crude, wooing you is like playing basketball with a porcupine. No compliment goes unpunished.”</blockquote><blockquote>I gave him a smile. I was aiming for sweet, but he turned a shade paler and scooted a bit farther from me. Note to self: work more on sweet and less on psycho-killer.</blockquote><blockquote>Curran looked back at me. “Why is it you always attract creeps?”<br>“You tell me.” Ha! Walked right into that one, yes, he did.</blockquote><blockquote>As he passed me, he leaned to Curran and handed him a paper fan folded from some sort of flyer.<br>Curran looked at the fan. “What?”<br>“An emergency precaution, Your Majesty. In case the lady faints.”<br>Curran just stared at him.<br>Raphael strode toward the Pit, turned, flexed a bit, and winked at me.<br>“Give me that,” I told Curran. “I need to fan myself.”<br>“No, you don’t.”</blockquote><b>Get me the next instalment! Quick!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405928334ra/10472755.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>• <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156913295" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bites</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1136556683" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 4</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222662503" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bleeds</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 5</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156907200" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Slays</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 6</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087380222" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Rises</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 7</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222671908" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Breaks</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 8</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088122695" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Shifts</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 9</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1388386563" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Binds</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 10</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767301739" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Triumphs</a> ★★★★</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_115087152" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115087152" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115087152?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">any UF fan who likes a kick-butt heroine</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=shifter">shifter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=desert-island">desert-island</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115087152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6192561192695730332"><br/>Remember when I said I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1811543.Magic_Burns__Kate_Daniels___2_' title='Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2) by Ilona Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magic Burns</a>? I might just love this book a little more. Just how good is it? Enough that it was my go-to when I was recently recovering from a headache--I wanted a dependable, awesome read and didn't want to start anything new that I'd end up hating.<br/><br/><u>Magic Strikes</u> is the third book in one of the best urban fantasy series out there. It maintains a very fast-moving plot with nicely developed characterization, has an unusual magic-technology premise, and stars a woman wh</span>
  <span id="freeText6192561192695730332" style="display:none"><br />Remember when I said I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1811543.Magic_Burns__Kate_Daniels___2_" title="Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns</a>? I might just love this book a little more. Just how good is it? Enough that it was my go-to when I was recently recovering from a headache--I wanted a dependable, awesome read and didn't want to start anything new that I'd end up hating.<br /><br /><u>Magic Strikes</u> is the third book in one of the best urban fantasy series out there. It maintains a very fast-moving plot with nicely developed characterization, has an unusual magic-technology premise, and stars a woman who is by far my favorite heroine.<br /><br />Kate's rescuing a banshee grandma for the Order of Knights of Merciful Aid when she's called to a shapeshifter murder. Security chief Jim tells her to butt out, but she accidentally spills the news to Curran the next day when she and Andrea, her best friend, are out at lunch. Once Curran the shapeshifter king is involved, events spiral fast and draw in a large cast of characters, including Saiman in his real form, Derek and an attractive female, and Raphael and Andrea in their elaborate mating dance. Jim has gotten himself and his security team in hot water. Kate joins with them to save the girl, the Pack, and their reputations in a secret underground fight club. A couple sections of this book were an emotional challenge, but in the end, I loved that Andrews aren't afraid to play rough with their characters. It's a risky move that adds tension to the story. <br /><br />The plot is non-stop action, but leavened with Andrews' trademark humor. I love the balance they achieve. Kate's humor is sometimes only for herself, sometimes for friends, but when faced with a serious situation, she is all business and no laughs.<br /><br />As usual, characterization is a standout. I love Kate's intensity as she fights in the parking lot, and as she stands up to Jim's stonewalling. In one, she uses her amazing fight skills, in the other, hard-won legal knowledge, shocking Jim. The character Dali is introduced in a way that would be comical if it wasn't so plausible and her other form so beautiful. Julie returns in a moving scene. This book contains some of my favorite scenes, including the scene with Rene the guard, the scene with Jim where Kate quotes the law, the bit with Raphael and the fan that makes me laugh every time, and several fight scenes. The antagonists are unusual characters in UF, believable in their level of ferociousness and able to provide formidable foes for the crew.<br /><br />Kate continues to be my favorite heroine.<br /><br />There's Kate and her feelings on vampires: <br /><br />"Part cult, part research institute, part corporation, all vomit inducing."<br /><br /><br />There's her opinion on inappropriate displays of emotion: <br /> <br />"Saiman picked up a coffee mug, stared at it, and hurled it against the wall. It shattered into a dozen pieces. We looked at him.<br />'Your date appears to be hysterical,' Rene told me.<br />'You think I should slap some man into him?'<br />Saiman stared at me, speechless. I had to give it to Rene--she didn't laugh. But she really wanted to."<br /><br /><br />Then there's her friendships:<br /><br />"'Kate?'<br />I have a superior reaction time. That was why although I shot out of my chair, jumped onto my desk, and attempted to stab the intruder into my office in the throat, I stopped the blade two inches before it touched Andrea's neck. Because she was my best friend, and sticking knives into your best friend's windpipe was generally considered to be a social faux pas.<br />Andrea stared at the black blade of the throwing dagger. 'That was great,' she said. 'What will you do for a dollar?'<br />I scowled.<br />'Scary but not work a buck.'"<br /><br /><br />Love it. <br /><br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/04/17/magic-strikes-by-ilona-andrews/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6192561192695730332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Athena Shardbearer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer"><img alt="Athena Shardbearer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546027968p2/4159427.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1052998198?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Athena Shardbearer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Athena Shardbearer" href="/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer">Athena Shardbearer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=its-all-shandras-fault">its-all-shandras-fault</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=kinda-want">kinda-want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=in-robin-i-trust">in-robin-i-trust</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1052998198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13877407336166645504"><br/><b>5 Stars AGAIN!!!!</b><br/><br/>You're so PURRRRRRR-fect, book.....I need you in my life...again.<br/><br/>---------------------------------------------------------------------<br/><br/>WOW!!! Kate Daniels, you're my new girl crush!!! I can't explain how refreshing and complete I feel after reading these books, and I can say that I'm a fan after reading this one. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>First, I wasn't a knight; I just worked for the Order of Knights of Merciful Aid. Second, negotiation wasn't my forte. I killed things. Quickly and with much bloodshe</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText13877407336166645504" style="display:none"><br /><b>5 Stars AGAIN!!!!</b><br /><br />You're so PURRRRRRR-fect, book.....I need you in my life...again.<br /><br />---------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />WOW!!! Kate Daniels, you're my new girl crush!!! I can't explain how refreshing and complete I feel after reading these books, and I can say that I'm a fan after reading this one. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>First, I wasn't a knight; I just worked for the Order of Knights of Merciful Aid. Second, negotiation wasn't my forte. I killed things. Quickly and with much bloodshed. Getting elderly banshees in denial off telephone poles wasn't something I did often.</b>
</i><br /><br />I don't know where I've been living for the past few years, but apparently its under a rock...because I wish I had started this series sooner. I have to admit, the first book is good..but not great. Book two was ok, but this one was PHENOMENAL!! I want to read it again and again, I mean they were traveling to this other dimension/world??? and the creatures and characters. I don't normally like the abundance of mythological characters or creatures of myth but Ilona Andrews does it just right...were its not too much or too little. I'm given a taste of what is to come without the lengthy descriptions. (A lot of the time when I don't know the history of a certain myth or mythological/religious creature I look it up.) <br /><br />Not only did this book satisfy what I look for in characters, but the world building, how real the places feel and how REAL the characters feel. OHHHHH....I love me some Raphael!!! And Saiman, I didn't like you in the beginning and now we're homies!! I was not expecting for him to be that AWESOME..just awesome. <br /><br />Now, the tension with Curran and Kate, I loves! I just love that she is not willing to give him what he wants even though she wants to. And I want her too! I mean the Beast Lord not getting what he wants, total Alpha Male, but I think he respects her more and its more worth while. <br /><br />The fighting scenes are INSANE!!! I love reading those scenes, when she releases Slayer to come out and play!! I can't even. <br /><br />Derek, my heart breaks for you but you need to quit getting your ass into shit you can't handle. Its like a little brother that picks fights with the bigger kids and comes to you to handle them. I love him, but sometimes....<br /><br />In all, this one is going into my favorites shelf. I need more Kate Daniels...I need more Ilona Andrews...and seriously, my ass will not miss anymore books signings when they come to town. They've been in my area three times this year. Athena, get your shit together!!! GAH!!!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cehbcNBaNZ50AISkHwGB70RFIkatFJIwT5iG7T3qzL5LzjKiawT89tMrMMXo9IswkhrFjmOZHFcU5sBc8Kk+JA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5pLmKO1z4YNypg300/m1pxEQ5Z+rhqzgT8gfsFLe2HDctI/6Vi0o69WNuZUkDL94x08CV2ULIocUtlkBn50q6g==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12308523782125583135">Ilona Andrews is the pseudonym for a husband-and-wife writing team. Ilona is a native-born Russian and Gordon is a former communications sergeant in the U.S. Army. Contrary to popular belief, Gordon was never an intelligence officer with a license to kill, and Ilona was never the mysterious Russian spy who seduced him. They met in college, in English Composition 101, where Ilona got a better grade</span>
  <span id="freeText12308523782125583135" style="display:none">Ilona Andrews is the pseudonym for a husband-and-wife writing team. Ilona is a native-born Russian and Gordon is a former communications sergeant in the U.S. Army. Contrary to popular belief, Gordon was never an intelligence officer with a license to kill, and Ilona was never the mysterious Russian spy who seduced him. They met in college, in English Composition 101, where Ilona got a better grade. (Gordon is still sore about that.)<br /><br />Gordon and Ilona currently reside in Oregon with their two children, three dogs and a cat. They have co-authored two series, the bestselling urban fantasy of Kate Daniels and romantic urban fantasy of The Edge.<br /></span>
